text:
I thought this was incredible!  I did make a few adjustments to the original recipe.  I used a three pound rump roast, only two packages (.67 oz each) of italian dressing mix and I put the entire jar and juices of the pepperoncini in with the roast from the get go.  I cooked it on high in the crockpot for 4 hours and then on low for 4-5 hours.  The meat just fell apart!  It was absolutley incredible!  I used french bread instead of buns, which I buttered and placed in a pan to brown.  I put some juice into a small bowl to dip the sandwich in.  Thank you for the recipe!

text:
We loved this recipe!  Extremely easy.  Changes for our tastes were:  We like spicey foods so I added another half jar of pepperoncinis--juice and all.   Added all peppers in half way thru the cooking process: after about 3-4 hours so the flavor soaked into beef.  Used 2 instead of 3 dressing mixes (from the advice of others). Brushed the hoagies very lightly with olive oil,   spinkled a bit of garlic powder & salt on them, toasted then added shredded meat and provolone & broiled until melted--(toasting the hoagies helped prevent them from getting too soggie when juice was poured over them) .  Put the hoagies in a bowl, added pepperoncinis to taste and laddled the unbelievable great juice over it.  Excellent!!!  I did go to great lengths after the meat was done to pull it out and shred it to make sure all the fat was removed and this took a LONG time. But this is not necessary just my preference.

text:
WOW - so simple and so delicious! This has to be one of the easiest and tastiest crock pot recipes ever! What's great about it too is it's very inexpensive and makes a lot. I added about 2 tsp. of minced garlic from the jar and used only 2 (1 ounce) packed of Good Seasons Italian dressing mix. Instead of a whole cup of water I used about 1/2 cup of balsamic vinegar to cut heat from the peppers and to cover more of the roast. I also added two vidalia onions that I quarted and added half way through cooking. I cooked this on low for 8 hours and the smell was heavenly. We served this on toasted hoagie rolls with provolone cheese. Everyone loved it! Thanks Randi for a great recipe!

text:
This is it! I'm from Chicago and since I do not  live there now, I forever crave THE Italian Beef sandwich. Only Chicagoans know what I'm talkin' 'bout. This recipe is as close as it gets. I read the other reviews first and altered the recipe accordingly. I bought a 1.75 lb. chuck roast. I used 2 C of Beef stock instead of water, 1 packet of dry italian italian salad dressing mix, 1/2 jar of pepperoncini juice (served the peppers on the side), 3 bulbs of garlic and I threw in some italian seasoning and addt'l Oregano. I could not insult this recipe by putting it on a hamburger bun, so I found some great pane rolls at the bakery and they were perfect. I cooked on high for 4 hrs and 2 more hours on low. My husband said this was the best tasting roast meat he has ever had. I will be making this recipe again and again. Thank you!!!

text:
My husband and I LOVED this!  My roast was around 2.7 lbs. and I only used 2 packets of Italian seasoning and added the peppers to taste, no juice.  We put provolone cheese on some hoagie buns and broiled them to toast the bread and melt the cheese.  We raved about them all through dinner!  I served it with a spinach strawberry salad and homemade baked french fries.
ALSO:  I try to share this secret with as many people as possible - when your meat is ready to be shredded, if you have a stand mixer (kitchen aid, bosch, etc)  put your meat in your bowl with your basic paddle attachment and turn it on low.  Your meat will be shredded in 20 seconds instead of slaving away with forks.

text:
I've used the dry Italain dressing mix in recipes before and found it way too salty for my taste. So, I made this recipe with a 2 lb roast, a 12 oz jar of pepperoncini, 2 cans of beef broth (can be low sodium), 1 TBL of Italian seasoning, 1 TBL oregano, and a few garlic cloves. I seasoned the roast with a little salt, and more generously with black pepper and granulated garlic. I cooked it for about 7 hours on high and it fell apart nicely. Try serving it on toasted French or Italian rolls brushed with garlic butter. I also add provolone cheese and sauteed sweet peppers. YUM!

text:
One suggestion that I would make to others is to use a sirloin tip roast rather than a chuck roast, making sure to give it plenty of time to slow cook. Using a sirloin tip roast eliminates all the fat and gristle that is common with a chuck roast, while still being a juicy and delicious piece of meat. As for the recipe, Iâ€™ve had better Italian beef in my day. While it was palatable, it was also little on the salty side when made as written. Next time I would add some dried herbs (oregano, Italian seasoning, etc) and back off of the dressing mixes by at least one packet if not two. Loved the peppers though!

text:
YUMMY!  Everyone in the house loved it.  I made own italian dressing spices from this website, and I added two beef boullion cubes. This is the one your looking for.   Here are the spices in case anyone else needs them. 2 T garlic salt, 2 T  onion powder, 2 T sugar, 2 T oregano, 2 t black pepper, 1 t red pepper, 1/2 t thyme, 2 t basil, 2 T parsley, 1/2 t celery salt (i used celery flakes), 2 T salt.  1/2 t lemon pepper (someone else mentioned it so I threw it in) I used these on a 3 pound roast,and it was perfect.  Fed 2 teenage boys, 1 hungry husband, 1 hungry 8 yr. old, and 1 picky meat eater...it was delicious.

text:
This is really good. I modify it just a bit by using Campbell's condensed beef broth, sauteed onions and half a jar of the pepperoncini peppers with half the juice. I serve this on toasted rolls with provolone cheese melted over the top. NOTE: If you have extra "au jus" from this recipe, it makes a great base for beef stew so don't waste it. Either make your stew the next day OR freeze it in a marked container for when you do make stew.

text:
I really wanted to give this 4-1/2 stars, but there's no button for that. I know real Italian Beef from Chicago and this is pretty close, but not quite there. I made a few modifications and that knocked down my rating. Instead of water, I used a full 2 cups of beef broth. Real Italian Beef is very wet. I also used a rump roast instead of chuck because it was on sale. I don't think there was any difference. I used only half a jar of pepperoncinos and only about half a cup of its juice. I'd rather allow diners to add some heat if they want. Also, I added some garlic and a little oregano and basil. And finally I recommend using hoagie or deli rolls instead of hamburger buns, that would make it more like the real thing. By the way, my favorite place in Chicago is Mr. Beef on Erie. Beats the beter known Al's in my opinion. This is a good version. I look forward to trying it again and adding my favorite extra - an Italian Sausage link.

text:
This is a wonderful recipe that has garnered raves!  Have made a few tweaks.  I only add 2 packages of the Italian dressing mix and reserve the third, use beef broth in place of the water, and add 4 to 5 cloves of garlic before slow cooking.  Once the beef is tender, I remove it from the slow cooker and shred it and mash the garlic cloves with it, adding enough of the cooking liquid and the reserved dry Italian dressing mix to taste (thus avoiding the "too salty" dilemma).  I slice onions very thin and put in a shallow bowl with enough of the crock pot liquid to cover, put plastic over the top and nuke for 1-2 minutes (until tender) - great flavor!  Melt provolone cheese on toasted rolls and serve with onions and pepperoncini - perfection!  Thanks, Randi!

text:
This is the recipe I've always used w/ a couple small changes - I use two seasoning packets and rub them into the meat before putting in the slow cooker. Instead of water, I use one can of beer. Gives it a little extra kick. I also put everything in the slow cooker all at once (instead of waiting to put the pepperoncinis in later). Instead of hamburger buns, I serve the beef on those little Pillsbury french rolls from the freezer section. They make the perfect sized hearty finger sandwiches. Add on a 1/2 slice of provolone cheese, and you're set!  Also, you should note that different brand names of peppercinis have different spicy-ness. I usually go for the mild one, but some brands don't offer a mild version.  People ALWAYS ask me for the recipe and it's SO easy!

For those of you with last minute meal plans, the chuck roast can be put in crock pot frozen, 2 pkg. Italain dressing mix, 1T. Oregano, 3/4T. basil, 2 Cloves garlic, minced,1 can beef broth instead of water and 3 whole pepperoncinis.  7-8hrs on med/low.  Served on any crusty roll with melted mozzarella and sliced pepperonci's!  Yum...

None
text:
This was really good. The French bread is a MUST. Any kind of soft bread like a hamburger bun or a soft hoagie will just get soggy and turn to mush. French bread is perfect for sopping up all of that delicious juice and it doesn't turn to mush in your hands while you're trying to eat it. I followed the recipe but made the following changes. I added two packets of no-sodium beef bouillon to the first cup of water, and only two packets of Italian dressing. Halfway through cooking, I took the meat out and shredded it. Added another pack of no-sodium bouillon, about a half cup of water and half of a third Italian dressing packet. I kept sprinkling it to taste. I cooked it from 11am until around 7pm, occasionally stirring and checking the broth to make sure it was not overly salty. It was perfect! The bouillon adds a good richness to the broth. Also, I added the entire jar of peppers with their juice, but I pulled the stems off first. This was a hit, will definitely make it again.

I just saw this recipe (08/05/16) on AR, but had a version of it given to me by my D-I-L, which I have made.  It is my favorite sandwich now.  However, I now prefer it made with a pork loin.  It keeps us away from red meat and is awesome!!  The recipe that was given to me, was different in that it called for a 4lb chuck roast, 15 oz can beef broth, 1 pkg Good Season Zesty Italian, 1 T. garlic powder, 8oz jar pepperoncini and 1 stick of butter.  Cook 8 hours on low.  Shredd and put back in pot.  Serve on bread of choice and top with provolone cheese or cheese of choice.  The next time I make it though, I will not use the butter for health reason...don't think it will affect the flavor that much.

text:
I have not been feeling well so my mom made this Italian beef for me. She took the time to trim the fat and it still came out super moist and tender (she did use a better cut of beef which made a huge difference- cuts from the chuck are all hugely different- this was probably a blade roast-not to be confused with the under blade roast-You can remove the connective tissue, which is ugly but perfectly fine to eat. It is tender, full of flavor, and juicy).  She cooked it for four hours on high and the meat was still very tough, so she finished cooking it on low for five more hours, adding the peppers and all of their juice when switching to low. My boyfriend makes a similar recipe, but cooks it overnight for 10 to 12 hours on low, then warms it when time to eat. His just falls apart in your mouth (though it's quite a bit more oily). The flavor is amazing. I  told her that I wanted her to make it again and again. Wonderful recipe!.....ok, she made it again with a lower quality chuck cut  and it wasn't nearly as tender, but the flavor was good-still, this time we were disappointed.******** One note on chuck roasts: if they are cone shaped, they are probably the mock tender muscle - and an inferior cut of chuck, tougher, stringier, and less flavorful.  Another inferior chuck cut is the shoulder-it's chewy and grainy and also lacks flavor. A chuck eye roast is another choice that is juicy and flavorful, but also very fatty. Finally, one more decent roast to try: the top sirloin.

region:

country:
None
text:
You must be careful, adding the pepperocini's and/or their juice really spices this up, like really.  I love it, but my family really won't eat it at that heat level.  To de-spice, stem the peppero's, remove the seeds and stem "meat" from the inside of the pepper and rinse well with water.  Drain and add during the last hour or so.  I add my own spices instead of prepackaged dressing mix, basil, oregano, fennel seed, thyme, juniper berry, peppercorn, bay leaf and whatever else strikes my fancy, couple of dashes of Worcestershire sauce and brown the meat first.  Also I add carrots, celery and onions (browned) and half a dozen garlic heads, smashed but not browned.

This was delicious!! One of the problems I have w/ trying slow cooker recipes is that they never quite taste as good as they smell. They always need more spices, and I'm not the type of cook that can say, "Oh, it needs a little bit of this...". I need to find recipes that taste great as they are. This recipe was VERY tasty! I prepared it exactly like the recipe. It was salty and spicy, which my husband and I both really like. However, if you want a little less salt, maybe decrease the italian seasoning mix until it fits your taste. If you like it a little less spicy, decrease the peppers, the juice, or leave them out entirely. I thought it was great as is!! I will definitely make this again!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Like other reviewers, I made a variation of this recipe which my whole family enjoyed: I used two packets of Wish Bone Italian Dressing mix, three beef bouillon cubes, and approx a tsp give or take of oregano, basil, garlic powder, onion powder, salt, and pepper.  Brought the water and seasonings to a boil and dissolved bouillon, then poured over meat in crock pot.  I set my device to high and after three hours, I cut the meat into approx 1-2 inch slices and submerged them in the liquid at the bottom of the crockpot.  After another six hours or so on low, I shredded the beef and returned it to the pot.  I set aside enough to feed my younger children, and then added one jar of pepperoncini's, including the liquid, to the meat in the crock pot.  The mixture was left uncovered on low heat until served, about 45 minutes.  I buttered and toasted hoagie rolls under the broiler.  I put the meat on the rolls and topped it with provolone, then slid them back under the broiler to melt the cheese.  Served these gems along with steamed beans and a cucumber salad.  A new recipe to add to the rotation, everyone loved this meal and it was super easy to make.

text:
Best thing by far I have made from this site so far. I was pretty skeptical, but it had almost the exact taste and texture of my favorite Italian beef from back home. I had a slightly smaller piece of meat than the recipe called for, so I reduced the amount of Italian dressing mix and I used half a jar of the peppers and juice, instead of a whole one. I also cooked it on low for about 10 hours, instead of high, just because I think meat comes out more tender that way. Agree with those who have said it's a waste to serve on a hamburger bun. Get yourself a good crusty roll of some kind. I topped mine with some sharp provolone and stuck it in the oven to crisp up the bread and melt the cheese. Fantastic.

text:
I saw these sandwiches featured on a Food Network show.  I have never eaten this before, but thought they looked delicious on TV.  I came across this recipe and read reviews etc and thought I would try it.  This meat was delicous and we absolutely loved it!!!!!    I had to make some changes since I decided to make it last minute, and will follow the recipe more closely next time, but it was still excellent.  I only had 1pk of dry italian dressing so I added bottled italian dressing from the fridge (about a cup) instead of the water.  I also added the pepperoncini's and juice 1/2 at the beginning and the other 1/2 at 4hrs in.  Cooked for 4hrs on high and then turned to low for about 4 hrs.  Toasted some delicious rolls under the broiler for about a minute, then piled some of the shredded beef and a thick slice of provolone cheese, back under the broiler for a min and serve with a salad.  My hubs went nuts over it!  I know he will be asking for this one again really soon!

text:
Loved it!  And hey I don't even have a slow cooker...I had a 1.5 lb. chuck roast, rubbed it down with the Italian seasoning first, placed on a rack in a roasting pan, in the oven 300 degrees for about 2.5 hours...tightly covered with heavy duty foil...it was a pretty fatty piece of beef, so the rack helped "drain" some of the fat.  Like others, I just dumped the whole jar of peppers and juice, along with some beef broth into the pan at the start.  Served on french hamburger rolls with some of the peppers chopped up...we were in heaven!  How Pittsburgh-y is this!

text:
I took the advice of some of the other reviewers and used only 2 .7oz packets of Italian dressing mix.  I also used a slightly larger roast (3.5 lbs) and used more than the recommended amount of water by 2-3x.  Unfortunately, it was still incredibly salty--maybe it was the brand I used?  That's not to say it wasn't extremely tasty, though!  Will definitely be making this again, but with further adjustments.  Will probably use just one (or one and a half) packet of Italian mix and more water to give ourselves more juice to dip in.  Also, I used only half a jar of pepperoncinis,  because I wasn't sure how spicy it'd be and I have a toddler to feed.  She isn't a beef eater, and this she actually ate most of!  Turns out the brand I used wasn't too spicy, so I'll probably use the whole jar next time since having more peppers in there might've been nice.  Even if this is or isn't close to authentic italian beef (I wouldn't know) it's still good!

Awesomely easy! I can't wait to make my sandwich when this is ready, so I just shred enough for my meal (on a toasted roll, with melted provolone or mozzarella).  When I'm done, the rest of it has cooled off enough to handle easily.  I drain the meat pretty thoroughly, and reserve the liquid in the fridge for my sandwiches (after I pick off the cooled fat) and then use the extra next time I make the recipe.  This is also FABULOUS with pork tenderloin.

text:
I made this recipe just as stated, only I had a larger cut of chuck roast.  I used 3 packets of the dressing and I added a whole jar, juice and all, of the peppers.  I added just a little water,and cooked it all day on low. It tasted great, not too salty.  The peppers just smashed into the meat easily.   I wouldn't recommend using the juice because it was very greasy, but maybe if you chilled it and scraped off the fat, it might be better.  It is easy, not too spicy, and both my kids don't complain when I make it.

text:
This is really easy and came out really good! I followed others' suggestions by paring back the Italian seasoning - I used 1 , .6 oz. packet on a 3 lb. roast.  I quartered two onions, placed them on the bottom of the pot, then added the roast, sprinkled the seasoning, added three cloves of smashed garlic,  8 oz. beer, 1/4 C red wine, and about 12-14 oz. of beef broth. Cooked on high for 6 hours, it shredded in the crock pot super easily, then cooked for another hour.  Toasted the buns, served with provolone and au jus. It was delic! Thank you Randi!

This recipe came out really well for me. I didn't find a 3 lb. roast so I used one that was slightly over 2 1/2 lbs. which worked out just fine for me. There was plenty of meat in this. I also used 2 packets of the Italian dressing mix instead of the 3 called for just because I felt it would be too much. I did not miss the third packet at all. I think two is definitely enough since I do not like my food too salty. I used a jar of sliced pepperoncinis because that's what I happened to have on hand. This came out really great tasting. I left all the juices in with the meat after shredding it because I didn't want it to be too dry. I would definitely make this again.

text:
Extremely yummy!  I used nearly 6lbs of beef and kept the original amount of dressing mix.  We made Philly cheesesteaks out of some of the meat.  For this we pulled out the roasts and let them rest/drain on a baking rack over a cookie sheet.  Once completely cooled we shredded and put half the beef with about 1/2 jar of pepperoncini's and pepperoncini juice in a slow cooker.  We removed most of the original liquid from the original slow cooker, then added the other half of the meat and the rest of the pepperocinis.  Everyone was able to make the sandwiches they desired from that point on.  I was one of the Philly Cheesesteak folks as I don't like the way Italian Beef sandwichs can be really soggy.  We also used bolillo rolls in place of hamburger rolls.

We will be making this again.  It was fabulous!

text:
Love this and make it often when company comes from out of town since it can sit in the crock pot while we are waiting on them to arrive. After reading all of the reviews and making it several times my favorite method is to rub the chuck roast with 2 pkgs of the Italian seasoning, cover with one cup of beef broth, add the pepperoncini and the juices and cook on low for 8 hours. Shred the beef and stir back into the juices in the crock pot. Serve on toasted hoagie rolls with provolone cheese.

text:
This was out of this world.  My whole family was addicted to this beef.  So much so I didn't have much leftovers.  The only thing I changed was I only used 1 pack of the italian seasoning mix.  Based on personal experience and other reviewers I was worried about it being too salty.  To compensate I added about 3 tsp of minced garlic, 1 T of dried oregano, 1/2 T dried basil, 1 T dried minced onion.   Also I drained the juice from the jar of peppers (it was a 12 oz jar as that was all I could find)  into the crockpot at the beginning and added the peppers the last 2 hours.  I wanted to make sure peppers weren't to soft or overcooked. Definitely going into our rotation!

text:
Really good
Changes: used 3 lb chuck roast with 2 packets of Italian dressing
DO NOT ADD EXTRA WATER!  IT GETS TOO SOGGY!
The key is to lightly coat buns with olive oil and garlic powder and then broil for one minute.
After shredding the beef do not put it back in the pot!!!  Put it directly on the bun.  It will be dry, not soggy.  Then top with provolone and broil for approx 45 seconds.

text:
I usually make this during the colder months and football season. Everyone loves it! The changes I made is instead of using water I use a light beer, I usually buy two packets but it only takes one to one and half packets of the dry salad dressing to run the meat with it. When putting into the slow cooker I first add the beer, half a jar of peppercini's then the meat. I let it go for six hours then I add half a jar of hot peppercini's and let it go for another hour to two hours depending on the tenderness of the meat. Once it's done I pull the meat apart with two forks and out it back in the slow cooker and mix it up and turn the slow cooker on low. I found through trial and error that either brioche buns and Kaiser rolls work the best. I like to use a garlic spread on the roll then meat then a slice of either provolone or add some mozzarella. Mmmhmmm it's the best!

text:
Just made this last week for just H and I.  We like leftovers so I used a 4# rump roast and 4 c. of 'no sodium' beef broth, taking advice from other reviews that it can become too salty.  I then added 2 packages of the dry Italian Dressing mix and about 2 T of powdered garlic, 1 T more of oregano, and one of Basil,and about 2 tablespoons of the juice from the pepperocinnis.  Allowed it to cook in the crock for the allotted time, shredded the roast and put it back in the crock with the juice.  I then added 2 green peppers and let those cook for about 20 minutes. (more time and they may have been mush)  Served on French rolls made for Italian Beef and H said it was absolutely the best he's ever eaten.  Ugh!!  Now wants me to make this once a week!  As good as this was, I do agree with others that the next time I will skip the pepperocinni juice until the end or even just add the peppers on individual sandwiches.  Somehow it altered the taste somewhat to throw it in at the beginning, for it to cook for hours.  Other than that this was absolutely excellent!  Thanks for the great recipe

After the meat was done there seemed to be a lot of liquid left.  I did double the recipe.  So I poured that into a container and set it aside.  I then dumped the jar of peppers liquid and all into the bottom of the crock pot, covered them with the meat, and turned the heat back on low for another hour.  I'm glad I set the broth aside, as when I used some the next day to reheat the leftovers it was more like gravy, which wasn't what I was after.  Great recipe.

text:
i LOVE this recipe!!  I've made it several times, so at this point, I have started to make a few adjustments based on my own tastes.  I prefer sirloin roast, b/c I hate beef fat.  It's usually lean enough, but I trim it if necessary.  Instead of water, I use beef broth and red wine.  I also add a couple of garlic cloves and a sliced onion to the liquid.  I also apread some of the Italian seasoning into the meat before I put it in the crock pot.  When it's cooked through, I pull it out and shred it with forks, then put it back in the crock pot and pour in 1/2 of a jar of pepperocinis.  When I used a whole jar, the juice was too spicy for me, even though the meat still tasted fantastic.  I like the roast aus jus to keep the meat moist.  After about 30 mins of additional simmering, it's ready to serve.

My family loves this Italian beef.  I follow the recipe as originally posted and do not find the seasoning to be overwhelming, just the opposite - perfect. This was a simple and amazing recipe. For those who like it a little more spicy, I just let the meat cook according to recipe, adding some jalapeno juice and pepperocini juices as well. Then once the meat was ready to shred, I shredded all of it up in a seperate bowl, without au jus, and added in some cumin, crushed red pepper, paprika, a half dozen drops of tabasco brand hot sauce, and about a half a dozen drops of a chile habanero hot sauce we had as well. After I poured in some of the au jus and mixed it all up. WOW. I unleashed on my guests and the look on their face was simply priceless. Best Italian beef they've ever had. So thank you for this recipe!

I had this at a shower a few weeks ago,my co-worker got the recipe from this site and it was FANTASTIC!!
